Local News Two

Yongshou Hua Firm Imports Diamonds, Evades Taxes 154

Smuggling and Tax Evasion Reaches Over 100,000 Yuan

Qiu Yongshou Transferred to Local Court

Yongshou Hua Firm Jewelry Store, located at 14 Henan Road, is owned by Qiu Yongshou, a native of Nanjing, specializing in the import and export of jewelry and diamonds. Around September of last year, Qiu ordered a large quantity of diamonds from abroad and successively shipped them to China. He dared to deceive customs and evade taxes. This has happened more than once to this day, with the total tax evaded amounting to over 100,000 yuan. Recently, the Jianghai Customs Tax Affairs Department discovered this. It secretly ordered the water police station to investigate and verify the facts. At 10:30 AM the day before yesterday, detectives Huang Songsheng and Cheng Yongnian, together with Hua detective chief Pang Ruiqing from the General Police Station, were dispatched to the address to arrest Qiu and take him back to the police station for detention. Inside Yongshou Hua Firm, 12 types of smuggled jewelry and diamonds, worth over 70,000 yuan, were seized. Due to the importance of the case, the police station feared the loss of evidence. It requested instructions from President Zhou of the First Special Court on how to handle the matter. President Zhou appointed Senior Clerk Wan Qian to go to the police station and hand over the seized items to the Westerner Bo Laidi Si, representative of the customs. Yesterday morning, the police station transferred Qiu to the First Criminal Court of the First Special Court. The police station's lawyer, Ru Bao Yi, explained the case and stated that the customs department requested the transfer of the defendant, which the police station did not oppose. However, the defendant hired lawyer Fan Gang to oppose the transfer. Judge Shen Bingrong reviewed and reported the case, and then ruled that Qiu Yongshou be allowed to be transferred to the customs for transfer to the local court. All seized items have been inventoried and handed over to the customs by this court.

According to another report, the firm's smuggling methods are quite ingenious. Because this type of jewelry is not like goods packed in large wooden boxes, these items are small and each person can hide values worth tens of thousands of gold coins. Therefore, each time the firm purchased jewelry from France, it was shipped to Hong Kong to avoid taxes. From Hong Kong to Shanghai, the firm sent people to wait in Hong Kong in advance. After the ship arrived, they hid the jewelry on their persons and returned to Shanghai on the same ship. Although the customs conducted strict inspections, no cases were ever cracked. This time, the discovery was beyond the firm's expectations. It is also heard that this case involves a Frenchman named Marce Juhan. Due to consular jurisdiction, after being detained, he was transferred to the French Consulate for review.

Continued Hearing of the Xu-Hu Lawsuit 155

Neither Plaintiff nor Defendant Appeared in Court

Defendant's Lawyer Presented Letters

Xu Jinping (also known as Zhongyi), a Jiahe woman who previously studied at Chizhi University, was betrothed by her family to Fengjing Ye Lishao. Later, she fell in love with Hu Bingheng in Shanghai. Although she married Ye, she maintained a friendly relationship with Hu, alternating between Ye and Hu for five or six years. It was not until last year that she formally divorced Ye. Lawyer Yang Changchi drafted a divorce agreement, stating that the boy, Duansheng, would belong to Ye but would still be raised by Xu until he reached the age of sixteen, when he would return to Ye's family. Ye would provide for his education. After Xu severed her relationship with Ye, she should have become closer to Hu, but the reality was quite the opposite. Not only did their relationship deteriorate, but lawsuits arose frequently. Xu initially filed a criminal complaint against Hu for abandonment and abuse, but it was rejected. Subsequently, she filed a civil lawsuit against Hu, requesting confirmation of her marital status with Hu and asking the court to order Hu to fulfill the contract and pay her 100,000 yuan in consolation money. During the previous hearing in the civil court of the First Special District Local Court, Judge Shen Hong, Xu's ex-husband Ye Lishao, suddenly appeared in court, proving that he and Xu had also fallen in love and married before divorcing. He argued that Xu should not use his son Duansheng as a tool to extort money from Hu. After the adjournment, he intended to accuse her of abducting his child and report her to the prosecutor's office, leading to a major conflict. They immediately reported each other to the criminal court. Although the case had been heard twice, it had not yet concluded. As for the Xu-Hu lawsuit, after it was rescheduled that day, Hu's lawyer, Chen Tingrui, based on the various facts discovered and Ye Lishao's testimony, submitted a written defense. The reasons were divided into two points: (1) regarding the request to confirm the status of wife, (2) regarding the request for consolation money. Regarding the first point, it was asserted that the two parties were merely concubines, and the status of wife was fundamentally untenable. Regarding the second point, it was stated that the document written by Hu was obtained by Xu through fraud and should be invalid according to the law. Yesterday morning, Judge Shen Hong held the tenth hearing. The gallery was full, but neither plaintiff nor defendant appeared in person. First, Weng Zhifan, Xu Jinping's lawyer, stated that the defendant had not provided living expenses since June of last year and had moved away the furniture in February of this year, effectively abandoning her. Witnesses could prove this. Hu Bingheng's lawyer, Chen Tingrui, immediately stated that the issue of status should be resolved first before investigating whether there was abandonment. Since the plaintiff did not appear in court and no evidence was presented, it was clear that there was no evidence. Therefore, the defendant would present counter-evidence. If the plaintiff still had evidence but had not brought it to court, it would be appropriate to adjourn the hearing. If it was merely empty talk, there was no need to postpone it. The plaintiff's lawyer continued, "They have been living together for six or seven years. How could there be no evidence? However, my lawyer cannot say for sure before contacting the client." Judge Shen then declared that if there was still evidence to be presented, the hearing could be adjourned; otherwise, the debate would begin immediately. Chen Tingrui immediately stated that all the defendant's important evidence, although previously stated in brief, needed to be presented in detail for the sake of clarifying the case. The most important point emphasized by the plaintiff was that she had the status of wife. The plaintiff had little education, and she sent hundreds of letters to the defendant. Therefore, if the letters related to her so-called status of wife were presented, the issue could be clarified and easily resolved. Chen's lawyer then submitted nine letters from Xu to Hu and explained the important points in each letter one by one. Regarding the first letter, he said that there were words of adultery in the letter. Since she admitted to adultery, she could not have the status of wife. The second letter instructed Hu on how to communicate to avoid being intercepted by others and asked Hu to give all the letters she had given him to Bing Ding. Such secrecy was not befitting of a wife. The third letter contained words such as "the die is cast, regret is useless," which should be the plaintiff's self-pity. The letter also summoned Hu, which showed that the plaintiff was enticing him. The fourth letter said, "Do not reply, for fear of leaking the news and hindering good intentions." If they were husband and wife, why would it be necessary? The fifth letter inquired about the only conclusive proof of their initial encounter on the Shanghai-Hangzhou train. The sixth letter could prove the origins of Rong and Duan, as Xu and Ye had also fallen in love and married before. Rong was born before marriage, and Duan was born after marriage. Ye Lishao had recognized him as his son, but Xu still claimed that Hu was the father. Hu initially did not know this secret. It was not until Ye appeared in court last time that he realized that Rong and Duan were not his children. The seventh and eighth letters were all about Rong and Duan, and were extremely clear. There was also a large package of letters after the ninth letter, which was too numerous to list. Therefore, it was not necessary to present them all. From the above letters, it was not difficult to understand that Hu and Xu had no marital relationship. The evidence of Ye and Xu's marriage and divorce, such as wedding invitations and divorce agreements, had also been presented previously. The agreement stated that Duansheng was Ye's son and was supported by Ye. Now she claimed that he was Hu's son and demanded money, which proved that she was a fraud. After the plaintiff filed the lawsuit, she claimed that she could not afford to pay the litigation fees and requested assistance. The money she had repeatedly extorted from Hu was considerable. It was previously deposited in a money shop, but now it had been withdrawn in full, amounting to over 10,000 yuan. How could she say that she could not afford to pay the fees? Therefore, her request for litigation assistance should be rejected if it had not been approved. If it had already been approved, it should be revoked to curb the unhealthy trend of cunning and contentious litigation. He also presented three passbooks as evidence. Then, Fei Yinshi, a Yangzhou woman who had worked in the plaintiff's house, testified that she had been employed by Xu Jinping since September 4 of the previous year and resigned on January 4 of this year. She called Xu "Grandma." There were only a young brother, a young sister, and Grandma in her family. In addition, there was a young master Chen who came every other day, usually in the afternoon, but never stayed overnight. The two children never called out to young master Chen. There was also a young master Pan who came every few months and always stayed overnight. Pan was from Nanhui, but after Pan came, Grandma always told me not to talk nonsense. This time, Grandma was involved in a lawsuit with young master Chen. I was found by someone to come to this place, etc. Xu's lawyer gave the woman a newspaper with photos of Hu and Xu and asked her who was young master Chen. The woman said that the printing was blurred and she could not identify them. Then, the plaintiff's lawyer stated that this woman was the plaintiff who recently accused Xu Jinping of abducting her son in the Second Special Court. Judge Shen asked about the reason for accusing Xu of abducting the child and announced that the case would be adjourned for further hearing.

Land Dispute Over Several Fractions of Land Lasts Nearly 30 Years 156

The Disputed Land Had Long Been Transferred

Lawsuit Resurfaces After Several Years

During the late Qing Dynasty and early Republic of China, Zheng Huahua and Jin Xiaoyun were unable to resolve a dispute over several fractions of land near the Nicheng Bridge. They sued in the former Mixed Court, which, after repeated investigations, rendered a decision on August 4, 1921. However, Zheng was still dissatisfied and requested a retrial, listing four items of claim: (1) return of the land, rejecting monetary compensation; (2) compensation of 1,341 yuan and 57 cents for land rent from the defendant; (3) reimbursement of 2,000 taels for litigation costs; (4) permission to collect the 1,000 yuan security deposit paid by the defendant as compensation for damages. The retrial of this case resulted in a decision on April 10, 1922, rejecting it for insufficient grounds. Subsequently, the Mixed Court was reorganized, and the Provisional Court simultaneously established an appellate court. Zheng then appealed to the appellate court. After reviewing the entire case file, the appellate court found that the appellant had not declared a reservation of appeal during the Mixed Court era, which was inconsistent with the agreed terms. The appeal was immediately rejected. At that time, Zheng accepted the verdict and did not declare an appeal again. Unexpectedly, Zheng Huahua had now died, and a woman named Zheng Wu, claiming to be Hua's wife, filed a retrial lawsuit with the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court, stating that after the judgment of the Mixed Court, her husband had submitted a petition to the Shanghai Daoyin's Office, but the office had not summoned him. There was now a draft of the appeal petition that could be used as evidence, and she requested that a retrial be granted. However, the defendant, Jin Xiaoyun, had also passed away many years ago, and his son, Jin Fenggang, hired lawyer Chen Tingrui to argue the case according to the law, listing six reasons. First, the issue of whether the main party applying for a retrial was qualified still needed to be studied, as the woman was actually being used and was a mere puppet, which was extremely hateful. Second, he thoroughly described the repeated trial and judgment process of this case. Finally, based on the precedents of the Supreme Court, he proved that it did not meet the requirements for a retrial and requested that it be rejected. The Second Branch of the High Court found that the arguments of both parties were contradictory and it was impossible to understand the truth without summoning witnesses for interrogation. During the initial hearing, Zheng Wu took the opportunity not to appear. The defendant believed that in order to clarify the truth, the woman must appear in court for questioning, so he requested that she be summoned. During the second hearing yesterday morning, the woman still did not appear. After Judge Hu questioned the witnesses who were present, he ordered the debate to begin. Then, the two lawyers representing Zheng Wu, Tao and Zhong, debated with the defendant's lawyer, Chen Tingrui, until the end. The official announced that the decision would be postponed to a later date. This case has been in litigation for nearly 30 years. The disputed land has long been transferred, but both parties still do not give up. It is truly the longest-lasting case in the First Special District.

Customs to Confiscate Ships in Violation 157

The Da Mei Wan Bao says that the steamship Bo Erxi Te, flying the British flag, arrived in Shanghai from Australia on August 9. The ship was carrying 75 dogs for the dog racing track, and unloaded them at a location near the Shanghai coast, and tried to transport them into the concession. The customs authorities discovered this, and now intend to announce the whole case. The ship is being held in port, and it is possible that it will be confiscated. According to Article 47 of the Treaty of Tianjin in 1858, British merchant ships are not allowed to sail to ports other than those opened up by the treaty, or to engage in improper trade along the coast. Any ship that violates this provision may be confiscated by the Chinese government, along with its cargo. It is heard today that the customs authorities will apply this provision to deal with the ship. The ship is 165 tons, built in 1911, and was originally a German coal carrier. It is currently registered in the name of Enkshi of the local Enkshi Company. Enkshi traveled to Australia a few months ago to drive the ship to Shanghai.

(6) Passengers who bring their own cars to the airfield must arrive at Longhua Airfield fifteen minutes before the scheduled flight time. (7) Passengers should note that the company's airfield is in Longhua, not Hongqiao Airfield. (8) Passengers should abide by all of the company's passenger regulations.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Thoroughly Investigates the Inferior Goods and Counterfeit Brands of the Printing and Dyeing Company 161

Believes Zhang Rongchu's Resignation is a Perfunctory Response

Zhang Rongchu, the manager of the Shanghai Printing and Dyeing Company, used inferior goods to counterfeit the company's products in an attempt to make private profits. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce immediately investigated and understood the details, which were reported in previous reports. Yesterday, the company sent a letter to the Chamber of Commerce, stating that it had approved Zhang Rongchu's resignation. The Chamber of Commerce believed that it had not earnestly fulfilled the layer of thorough investigation according to law and did not approve the company's request. The original letters are recorded below: (1) Letter from the Printing and Dyeing Company: To the esteemed members of the Standing Committee of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, I am writing in response to your kind letter. Our association convened a meeting at 2:00 PM yesterday to approve the resignation of General Manager Zhang Rongchu pending investigation. The company has compiled all the original blank contract orders and decided to publish them in major newspapers from today onwards. At the same time, the company has publicly appointed managers Chen Zhibi and Xie Qingqing to be fully responsible for all company affairs. We hope that your association will guide and maintain us in the future. We look forward to it. (2) Reply from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce: We received your letter on the 25th of this month, stating that Zhang Rongchu's resignation has been approved, and the orders have also been announced. Please maintain the exports as usual, etc. It was submitted to the ninth standing committee meeting for discussion, and it was decided that the first point of the three points resolved by the Executive Committee, that Zhang Rongchu should be thoroughly investigated according to law, has not been earnestly fulfilled, and only the approval of resignation pending investigation is a perfunctory plan. The request is not approved. The corresponding record is sent back in a letter, please check.

Bean and Rice Industry Decides to Stop Shipping Xiangmao Reserved Rice 164

Because of What? Slandering the Reason of Da Youheng

The Shanghai Bean and Rice Industry Association convened an emergency meeting of colleagues yesterday afternoon, because the northern industry colleague Da Youheng booked Cheng Xiaojiao rice from Xiangmao Foreign Firm, and discussed a temporary delay in delivery. Unexpectedly, the foreign firm posted a notice slandering Da Youheng for closing down, and sued the court for sealing. At the meeting Da Youheng reported that previously, on behalf of the customer, one hundred tons of Cheng Xiaojiao rice was booked from Xiangmao Foreign Firm. The rice arrived in port, just after the incident, when the financial situation was suspended, so the foreign firm was discussed a temporary delay in delivery, and the warehouse rent and interest were acknowledged. Unexpectedly, Xiangmao Foreign Firm published an advertisement the week before last, slandering Da Youheng for stopping business, and it was in the process of negotiation. Unexpectedly, the foreign firm sued the local court to seal my firm, causing long-term losses in business. The rice that was previously booked is calculated in accordance with the current market, and the warehouse rent and interest only amounted to over a thousand taels. At that time, it was acknowledged, and the advertisements published in the newspaper were reviewed, and the colleagues were very angry. The colleagues in the industry all have fixed foreign rice in trade with Xiangmao Foreign Firm. Now the amount of rice fixed by Da Youheng is very small. Xiangmao Foreign Firm published advertisements slandering the closure of business and sued the court to seal Da Youheng. This matter is related to the harm to all colleagues in the industry. After discussion by the public, it was decided that the rice purchased from Xiangmao Foreign Firm by my colleagues would be suspended for shipment from today. After this case is over, a method will be decided, and a letter will be sent to the Miscellaneous Grain Association to notify colleagues of various gangs. Da Youheng should file a counterclaim with the court, and my colleagues should unanimously help. For the goods traded by the Miscellaneous Grain Association between colleagues and foreign merchants, the foreign merchants all use Western characters to make the bill of exchange, and the association is currently striving to negotiate to write all the bills of exchange for goods ordered with foreign merchants in Chinese, and that will be effective.

Liu Ruiheng Reports on the Recent Situation of Cholera in Shaanxi and Henan 165

To Zhu Qinglan's Letter

Since the beginning of summer this year, cholera has been most prevalent in the disaster areas of Shaanxi and Henan provinces. Previously, Zhu Ziqiao, director of the Disaster Area Work Group of the National Government's Flood Relief Committee, repeatedly telegraphed Liu Ruiheng, director of the Nanjing Health and Epidemic Prevention Team, asking him to send doctors and medicines to treat them as soon as possible. The letter from Liu is recorded below, so that the general public can read it and know what to prevent.

Zi Qiao Sir, I acknowledge the frequent attention to the prevention of cholera in the two provinces of Yu and Shaanxi. I have repeatedly replied to you. I have also invited you to see it. Now I have received a letter from Sun Runchen, the technical officer sent by this department to guide epidemic prevention in the two provinces of Yu and Shaanxi. The member investigated in detail in Tongguan, Xi'an, Lintong, Weinan, Huazhou, Huayin, and other cities, villages, towns, and forts. The reason for the rampant cholera this year, in addition to flies as the medium of infection, is especially important, because the public does not understand the importance of isolation and disinfection. Therefore, when one person is sick, all relatives who are attending to the illness and visiting the sick, and those who are in contact with washing the patient's clothes, are infected with the disease, and the infection spreads, and it becomes a prairie fire. The member has already drafted simple chapters and propaganda methods and handed them over to the Shaanxi Epidemic Prevention Committee to promote and publicize, so that the public can understand the importance of isolation, in order to reduce the path of infection. In Tongguan County this time, it is estimated that about 800 people died and about 3,000 were infected. The matters that should be handled in the prevention of cholera previously telegraphed to the province by this department have been handled in order, and the department will assist in 5,000 bottles of cholera vaccine for preventive injections. It is found that the deaths of patients in Tongguan and Xi'an have been reduced. In Henan, the number of counties reporting the epidemic has reached more than 30, and the area near Luoyang is the most severe. The central government agencies in Luoyang, together with the local organization of the Xingdu Epidemic Prevention Committee, are actively carrying out all prevention and control work. The member and the physician Niu Zengshu, who was previously sent to Luo by this department, stayed in Luo separately and went to other epidemic areas to guide prevention and control. The department assisted in 3,000 bottles of vaccine, which were allocated in batches for preventive injections. Health inspector Yang Qixiong was transferred to various epidemic areas today to guide the local creation of disinfection work for well water and drinking water. After becoming proficient in one place, he would be transferred to other places for guidance, and the local learning staff would continue to handle it, in order to make it universal. I am concerned about the public's suffering, and I am always concerned about the epidemic situation in the Central Plains. I am very pleased to tell you about one or two. I respectfully wish you peace, your brother Liu Ruiheng. August 20.

### Hadong Estate Case - Plaintiff Appeals 167

According to the Zi Lin Daily, besides the lawsuit filed by Ezra Hadong, another Hadong residing in Mumbai also started a lawsuit through lawyers in Shanghai. After the British Court ruled against him, the Mumbai Hadong also filed an appeal. Yesterday, the attorney representing Mrs. Hadong, the defendant, requested the British Court to order the appellant to pay a deposit of 6,000 yuan within 14 days to cover court expenses. After hearing the arguments from both sides, the judge granted the request, ordering the appellant to pay the deposit within 14 days from yesterday in order to proceed with the case.

### Opening Ceremony of Jiqun Branch Hospital in Pudong 168

In Gao Hang Town, Pudong, a hospital was established due to the discovery of an epidemic. Local figures requested Mr. Du Yuesheng to donate funds for the establishment. The hospital opened on the 10th of this month, and a formal opening ceremony was held the day before yesterday. More than 200 people attended, including Du Yuesheng's representative, Pan Hongding, the Health Bureau representative, Sun Jiaqi, the director of Jiqun General Hospital, Xiang Yumin, Zhao Dixian from the Gaoqiao Municipal Committee Office, and representatives from various organizations. Yu Xingqiu, Pan Hongqi, Gao Kechang, and others warmly received them. The ceremony was held at 10 a.m., chaired by Hongding, recorded by Ye Yiyi, and hosted by Pan Hongqi. The ceremony proceeded as planned. First, Hongding, representing Director Du, reported on the opening process. Then, Yu Shineng, the director of the hospital, reported on the hospital's status, stating that since its opening, the average daily number of patients has been over 300, which shows the urgent need for the hospital. He hoped that local figures and the government would support the hospital permanently. Next, Yu Xinghui, representing the sponsors, reported on the preparation process and the hospital's financial status. Subsequently, guests Yuan Zhe and Ge Jiuru delivered speeches and took a group photo before dismissing.

### A Pedestrian Hit by a Bus 169

Su Rentao Genlong, a 19-year-old apprentice at Yulong Rice Shop at No. 999 Changan Road, Zhabei, was riding a bicycle around 4 p.m. yesterday when he was passing Xinqiao, Shanbanchang. He was suddenly hit by a speeding No. 10 bus. Unable to avoid it, he was knocked to the ground and sustained head injuries. He was sent to Renji Hospital for treatment but died. The hospital then transferred the body to the coroner's office for examination.

### Two Suspects Arrested in Wuxi for the Kidnapping of Pu Wenting 170

Detectives from the Special Branch of the French Concession Police arrested three kidnappers, Zheng Shifan, Zhang Afu, etc., in connection with the kidnapping of Pu Wenting and Qian Shanguan. They were handed over to the court to await further investigation. According to Zheng et al., two accomplices from Wuxi, Gao A'da (aka Niu Bitou A'da) and Chen Liangqing, were hiding in Wuxi. Inspector Jin Jiulin dispatched Detective Zhang Ziying, along with Patrolman Cui Zhenguo, to Wuxi. Together with the Public Security Bureau, they arrested Gao and Chen and brought them to Shanghai. Yesterday, they were handed over to the Second Special Court. Judge Wang presided over the first criminal court for the interrogation. The police attorney, Fei Xizhen, explained the case, stating that the two defendants were involved in the kidnapping of Pu Wenting and were brought from Wuxi with the assistance of the Public Security Bureau. He requested a postponement for a joint trial with Zheng Shifan et al. The court briefly questioned the defendants. Gao claimed to be a sock maker in Wuxi, and Chen claimed to be a clerk for a lawyer. Both claimed that they had never committed

Page 16

any crime and hired Attorney Zhu Kuangming for defense. The judge postponed the trial to August 31 and ordered it to be merged with the extortion case of Zheng Shifan et al.

The defendants were temporarily detained at the police station.

### Monks of Yishou Chan Temple Violate Monastic Rules 171

A Buddhist Sanctuary

Turns into a Den of Iniquity

The Yishou Chan Temple, commonly known as Zhu Tianjun Temple, is located on Gansu Road behind the First Special District Court. It usually attracts many worshippers, especially those who participate in flower lotteries. The abbot of the temple, Qian Guang (aka Fa Kun), is addicted to opium. He has set up a smoking set in his Zen room upstairs, where he reclines and smokes. More than ten of his monks are also addicted and have beds and opium sets in their rooms. When there are Buddhist services, benefactors who are addicted to opium are also welcome to go upstairs for a smoke. The price of opium, regardless of the amount, is left to their discretion. As a result, the upstairs of the temple is filled with smoke and stench. Yao Jialin, the Chinese inspector of District C of the Hongkou Police Station, learned of this and secretly investigated the temple. After confirming the facts, he reported to the Special Court and obtained a search warrant. He went to the temple at 9 a.m. the day before yesterday and went straight upstairs, where he found three rooms with people smoking opium and taking red pills. He arrested the abbot Qian Guang, the guest monks Lin Qiang, Pu Qing, Miao Xing, Ke Jin, Hua He, and the servant Wu Ashou, totaling seven people. He confiscated six opium pipes, four opium lamps, one pound and thirteen ounces of raw opium, two bags of opium paste, a large number of red pills, opium dregs, opium trays, two vats of opium paste, as well as tonic bird's nests, white fungus, deer antlers, yellow croaker paste, and silver dollars. He took everything to the Huisi Police Station for detention. Yesterday morning, they were handed over to the Second Criminal Court of the First Special Court. Police Attorney Wang Yaotang stated the above facts, stating that the defendants were monks and should abide by the monastic rules. However, they openly smoked opium in the Buddhist sanctuary, transforming it into a den of iniquity. He requested severe punishment and asked for the temple to be sealed. Inspector Yao reported the circumstances of the arrest, stating that he had personally investigated the temple's neighbors and sent women disguised as worshippers to smoke opium before making the arrests. He presented the opium sets and opium paste as evidence. When questioned, all defendants except Hua He and Wu Ashou admitted to smoking opium. Judge Wu Tingqi verified the confessions and sentenced Qian Guang (aka Fa Kun) to three months of imprisonment and a fine of 300 yuan. Hua He and Wu Ashou were found not guilty. The remaining four, Lin Qiang et al., were sentenced to two months of imprisonment and a fine of 20 yuan each. The opium paste and opium sets were confiscated, and the remaining items were returned. The police station should file a separate request for the temple to be sealed.

### Daxin Silk and Satin Bureau Enthusiastically Promotes Domestic Goods 173

Daxin Silk and Satin Bureau, located at the corner of Shilu and Sanma Road, has always been dedicated to promoting domestic silk and satin and regaining control of interests. Since the January 28 Incident in Shanghai, the bureau has increasingly felt that the way to resist Japan and save the country is to actively promote domestic goods. It has successively ordered dozens of kinds of new and fashionable fabrics from famous domestic factories. The fabrics are durable, have a rich texture, and are affordable, which appeals to the general public. At a time when the social economy and people's purchasing power are weak, the bureau's order is sure to be well received. This is not only a celebration of the bureau's business development but also good news for the promotion of domestic goods. It is said that the ordered goods of various colors have arrived in Shanghai one after another, and the bureau is selling them at discounted prices to ensure sales.

### Death of Revolutionary Pioneer Lin Zhihua 174

Revolutionary pioneer Lin Zhihua, who used to work at the Minli Daily, was known for his efforts in the revolutionary cause. He provided financial assistance to many comrades in need. Most of his assets were spent on this. After the national situation was roughly settled, he retired and lived at home. Recently, his old illness recurred, and he died in his Shanghai residence at No. 1146 Gordon Road the day before yesterday, despite medical treatment. Everyone who heard the news mourned his passing.

### Invention of the Automatic Duplicator 175

Song Zijiang's newly invented automatic duplicator (i.e., offset plate) has been patented by the Ministry of Industry of the National Government. It can be written on ordinary paper with a fountain pen, brush, or pencil in one color or five colors. When printed with this device, it can produce 150 copies in three or five colors in one step. Recently, it has been used for school lectures, agency

telegrams, and public association publications due to its reasonable price and ease of use. The Shanghai management office is located at China Industrial Company, No. 9 Hankou Road, telephone 13734. You are welcome to visit and try it.

### Clearance Sale at Civilization Bookstore 176

Store Site Also to Be Sold

The main distribution center of Civilization Bookstore on Nanjing Road in this city has announced its closure and is selling off all kinds of inventory at discounted prices, such as books, rubbings, records, mirror frames, screens, paintings, etc. Many of the bookstore's products are excellent, especially the rubbings and paintings, which are exquisitely made. The discounted price is only 10% to 60% of the original price. A clearance sale department has also been set up to display books of foreign and domestic editions accumulated over the years, with particularly low prices starting from a few copper coins, some being less than 10% of the original price. There are also large quantities of fountain pens being sold at extremely low prices, which are rarely seen in the market. As a result, the store has been crowded with customers in recent days. It is said that the bookstore is about to close and has decided to sell off the store site and equipment. Nanjing Road is located in the center of the city, and the bookstore is located in the center of Nanjing Road. The location is excellent and unparalleled, making it a great place for business.

It was requested to discuss whether to approve the request. It was resolved to reply by letter from the secretariat and instruct the members to submit detailed regulations and the number of members joining the class for review, so that it could be submitted to the next meeting for discussion. (8) A submission from the 34th branch requested improvement of the messenger holiday incentive method and suggested that messengers who do not take sick leave throughout the year should be given a bonus of one month's salary, and that those who have taken sick leave should have it deducted according to the number of days. (9) How should we express our opinion regarding Lin? It was requested to discuss. It was resolved that: 1. The principle was unanimously approved; 2. The method (confidential). (10) Committee member Yan proposed that the library should be restored as soon as possible due to the needs of members. It was resolved to elect comrades Cheng Zuoqing and Shui Xiangyun as director and deputy director of the library, and the director and deputy director would hire five people (not limited to committee members of the union) to form a library book purchasing review committee. (11) Committee member Fan proposed that the badges for the current executive and supervisory committee members should be issued as soon as possible for identification, but whether the previous style should be improved was requested to be discussed. It was resolved that the Standing Committee should order the art department to draft an artistic style for the badges so that they could be made quickly. (12) Committee member Wang proposed that Tian, the administrator of the mechanical workshop supervisory office, repeatedly suppressed members without reason, requesting a thorough investigation and punishment to serve as a warning to others. It was resolved that the investigation department should investigate and handle the matter. (13) Committee member Cao proposed that low-level members withdrawn from the Northeast have very low salaries, and the General Administration should be requested to solve the accommodation problem to maintain their livelihoods. It was requested to discuss whether this was feasible. It was resolved that the negotiation department should negotiate. The resolutions were read and revised, and the meeting adjourned.

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated: Cloudy skies over the Shandong coast and the Yellow Sea, with fairly strong northeasterly winds. Free Talk

Random Notes

Taboo of the Zhan Lu 184

— Zhan Lu

Many of the taboos passed down are a kind of traditional social superstition.

Westerners avoid the number thirteen. We Chinese do not need to avoid the number thirteen. However, those who are infatuated with Westernization must also avoid thirteen for a moment, as a modern habit of showing off. People from Yan avoid saying forty-five, as recorded in Wu Yifeng's "Xun Zhi Tang Za Chao":

"People from Yan avoid saying forty-five. If someone asks them, they do not say, 'Last year I was forty-four years old,' but instead say, 'Next year I will be forty-six years old.'"

People from Lu avoid saying forty-one, as recorded in Wang Xiaoyin's "Fu Xuan Xu Yu":

"There is often a kind of vulgar saying among the common people that people compete to avoid it. For example, when a person reaches the age of forty-one, they avoid saying it. If someone asks, they answer with evasive words, or simply say the taboo year directly, without any understanding, which is quite laughable." This passage describes the customs of Shandong province.

People from Wu avoid the word "slave" by using the word "nose," as recorded in Chu Bunong's "Jian Hu Ji":

"In Wu customs, the word 'slave' is avoided by using the word 'nose.' The explanation is: 'To decorate the facade.' Or it is said: 'The elephant's nose can touch people, and the pig's nose is good at digging the ground,' which means causing trouble."

People from Zhejiang avoid the word "duck," as recorded in Zhuang Chuo's "Ji Lei Bian":

"People from Zhejiang greatly avoid using 'duck' as a name. Ducks only have one male, and although they mate, there are no eggs. Two or three males are needed to have offspring. It is believed that the taboo is because of this."

Among the various taboos mentioned above, the Wu custom of avoiding "slave" by using "nose" is now rarely seen. Occasionally, when talking about servants, the words "tip of the nose" are still used instead. The Zhejiang custom of avoiding "duck" is also no longer the case. However, the author of "Ji Lei Bian" lived in the Song Dynasty, so what he said was naturally the custom of the Song people. This reminds me of the novel "Water Margin," where Yun Ge treats Wu Dalang as a fat duck. Wu Da said, "My wife doesn't steal men, so how am I a duck?" According to this, the Song people avoided "duck" in a way similar to how people today avoid "turtle." And the place where it was avoided was not limited to Zhejiang province. Wu Da was from Qinghe County, Shandong, and he also knew to avoid "duck," which shows that the custom of avoiding "duck" was very common among the Song people.

Japanese Troops Are Not to Be Feared 185

— Wang Quchang

The Japanese bandits have been deeply invading us for eleven months now. Those who plan for the country are only intimidated by their past ferocity and dare not speak of war. They say that ten days is enough to destroy our country, or even that it cannot be defended for even one day. One voice echoes another, forming an unbreakable consensus. Even if there are one or two loyal and brave men who are aroused by righteous indignation and rise up, they seem to deeply agree with it, but are actually deeply afraid of it. Therefore, they ultimately hesitate between peace and war. Now the Japanese have invaded Rehe and are spying on Pingjin. Although those who plan for the country speak of uniting to resist the invasion, I fear that they may still be intimidated by their ferocity and procrastinate, causing mistakes. Therefore, I cite past events and solemnly tell them: Facts ultimately prevail over empty words. What is there to fear about the Japanese? In the Sino-Japanese War of 1894-1895, in the Battle of the Datong River, Ma Zhongwu, with a few thousand exhausted soldiers, faced more than 20,000 stubborn Japanese troops, and was also trapped in a heavy encirclement. The situation was precarious, but Ma's army ultimately broke through the encirclement and achieved excessive casualties. And in the Battle of Incheon, Ye Zhichao also broke through the encirclement with 2,000 weak soldiers and returned to Pyongyang. Are the Japanese really good at fighting? Are we really unable to fight? This is one point. In the Battle of Pyongyang, our army used 15,000 men to defend against the invading bandits, but only 8,000 were actually capable of fighting. Moreover, the generals were timid, the soldiers were lazy, the land was vast, the forces were divided, and the command was not unified. The enemy attacked with five times the number of troops. It seemed that they could not hold on for a moment. However, they still fought fiercely for four days before being defeated. Are the Japanese really capable of defending? This is the second point. Their defeat against Russia was not because the Japanese were able to win. Russia actually defeated itself. Before the war, it was already full of holes and sores, and it was exhausting and far from its base. Those who knew the situation had long concluded that there was no chance of victory. However, the Japanese still repeatedly fell into bitter fighting, suffering as many as 200,000 casualties. The chieftain Ooyama Iwao was so ashamed that he committed suicide, and the chief of staff Kodama Gentaro even prayed to the east every day, begging for blessings. It can also be seen that their strength was exhausted and they were begging for help. This is the third point. However, this is still a matter of the past. Some people think that it cannot be discussed today. In the Jinan Incident in 1928, our army's city defenders were only 500 men. The bandits attacked with twice the number of troops but ultimately could not succeed. Afterwards, when our army withdrew and broke through the encirclement under orders, the bandits were almost defeated. At that time, a reporter from the Osaka Asahi Shimbun in Japan described the embarrassment of their army in a telegram. The chief of staff Kuroda Shuroku saw it and was greatly ashamed and angry, accusing him of not loving the country and not being able to conceal their military affairs. (This is according to Gong Junde's words). This is enough to show the uselessness of their army. This is the fourth point. As for the Battle of Shanghai, the Japanese倾 country with half of its forces to deal with one corner, and even changed its commander four times. This is even more obvious and needs no further discussion. This is the fifth point. The Japanese have a conscription system. The soldiers are mostly from the middle class and are accustomed to comfort. When they leave their families, they tearfully plead for safety and pray to the gods for blessings. They are no longer the fierce warriors who prayed for death in the past. Therefore, once they are trapped in bitter fighting, they flee together. This can be seen from the battles of Shanghai and the Northeast. This is the sixth point. Moreover, since the Japanese won against Russia, they have not encountered a major enemy. Generals below the rank of lieutenant general indulge in armchair strategy and have never been trained in battle. They are also mired in inertia and given to lasciviousness. Every time they send troops, they take geishas with them. An army goes out with discipline. Do the Japanese really have discipline? This is the seventh point. Considering the past, it is like that. Examining the present, it is like this. If they cannot fight, cannot attack, and cannot go out with discipline, but only rely on their superior weapons and arrogance to try to succeed, what is there to fear about them? The Xuanju ant has its advantages. When the ant's nest is destroyed, and the red ants spy at the door, it must use its clan to bite and kill them, eventually staying far away from the leeches. If there is no mutual assistance, then the stupid people must have something to protect them. Now the spies at the door are approaching. If we cannot be like the Xuanju ant to bite the enemy, but want the people to protect the broken nest, how can we get it? Alas! Can we be inferior to the Xuanju ant? Moreover, they are not even worthy of fear.

The Silver Car of the Overseas Chinese 186

— Huanhua

The progress of extravagance among the people of Shanghai in recent years can be described as rapid. However, due to the many hidden dangers lurking, they cannot help but be cautious and dare not make any excessive moves. Otherwise, with the kind of flamboyant big bosses and young masters, the use of silver cars as a form of display would have happened long ago, and they would never have allowed other places or other families to enjoy such exclusivity first, right?

I have a friend who does business in Penang, and we recently reunited after a long separation. He told me a strange story:

Many of the overseas Chinese businessmen in Penang have become rich through business. Among them, a Mr. Chen from Quanzhou, Fujian, has accumulated more than ten million in assets. He is naturally fond of spending and enjoys everything to the extreme. A few years ago, he suddenly had a whimsical idea and ordered a silver-shelled car from a famous British car factory at the cost of 300,000 gold coins. Soon, the car arrived, causing a sensation in the local community.

On the first day he rode in it, a small twist occurred. As he was riding in the silver car from his residence to his company to do business, a policeman stopped the car and said to him: "The police chief requests Mr. Chen to have an important matter to discuss in person." Chen and the police chief had a personal relationship. Since the police chief requested his presence, he could not refuse, so he ordered the driver to drive the car to the police station.

Upon entering, a guard led him to the waiting room. He was shocked because he had never broken the law. What was the reason for this? Before long, he was questioned. The police chief said as soon as he saw him: "I have received orders from the governor that Mr. Chen is too extravagant and actually rides in a silver car, which is more excessive than the English emperor. He should be charged with a corresponding crime." Mr. Chen argued, "If silver cars are not allowed, and riding in silver cars should be prohibited and punished, please show me which article and item of the law states this. I am a law-abiding businessman who has never broken the law. There is no reason for the government to detain me. Although the police chief claims that it is the governor's order, there is no specific article for punishing extravagance. Therefore, what kind of judgment should be made for the governor's defamation of a law-abiding citizen's reputation and infringement of a law-abiding citizen's freedom? I am a person in business and my time is very valuable. I cannot stay here for long. Moreover, I must ride in the silver car." Chen was fluent in English and spoke very reasonably. Nearly a thousand people were listening and nodded in agreement. The police chief hesitated for a while before agreeing to report to the governor for instructions. Later, he announced: "Mr. Chen's use of a silver car for transportation is not what a law-abiding person should have. However, considering that there is no illegal behavior, he is exempt from punishment." Mr. Chen finally won the case and continued to enjoy his silver car in peace.

A Student Obsessed with Detective Novels 187

— Laoren

Martial arts novels have the strongest influence on young people's minds. Newspapers often report news of young people leaving home and going to the ends of the earth to find sword-wielding immortals and knights, which is enough to prove it to us. However, the reality is becoming more and more bizarre. A senior high school in Jiaxing County, Zhejiang Province, recently discovered a student who was so obsessed with reading detective novels that he committed crimes and had wild ideas, setting fires in the school building more than ten times. It was not until several months later that the case was solved. He told the principal, "Although I unfortunately failed, I am very proud. On the one hand, it can prove that the school authorities' detective methods are immature. For me, who has rich experience, it is naturally not easy to subdue me." This kind of strange thing can truly be said to be unprecedented. The school is one of the most famous high schools in Zhejiang Province and was founded entirely with funds raised by Christians. At the beginning of the spring semester of this year, there were several consecutive fires in the school building. The brand-new library suffered heavy losses due to the visit of the god of fire. The school authorities took all kinds of precautions but still could not avoid it. They had to encourage all students to pay attention and observe secretly at all times. Over time, not only was the case not solved, but it became more and more serious. Fires were also reported in the most secluded places in the school. This caused panic and confusion among all the students. They organized a patrol team to patrol day and night. On the one hand, they were afraid that it was the work of fox spirits, so they had to set up an altar and offer fresh fruits every day, hoping that they would stop playing jokes. Who knew that one night, several students went to the playground for a walk. Suddenly, they saw a child setting a fire. They thought that the opportunity was not to be missed, so they rushed forward and grabbed the arsonist. Upon closer inspection, it turned out to be a junior high school student. He said that the arson was entirely instigated by a senior high school student. His only purpose for setting the fire was to test in the field whether the average person had the ability to solve the case, completely indulging in detective novels. After receiving the confession, the school authorities immediately expelled the detective novel enthusiast. From then on, the bizarre fire disappeared without a trace.

Secret History of the Twenty-One Demands (4) 188

— Si Pin

Moore and Donner returned from their trip to the East and were very alarmed when they learned of this matter. Tong came to see me with them. Moore was very angry that his assistant had sent such a telegram to the United States without verifying it with Heki. Donner also took a copy of the Twenty-One Demands and said to me that he had been severely questioned by the consulate for this matter. As a result, both of them resigned from their positions in London and New York.

Moore had shown the Twenty-One Demands to Heki. Heki strongly denied it. However, Moore had already found out the source of the news and was convinced that the demands were real. Therefore, I also went to visit Heki, knowing that he would also deny the matter to me. I first sent my secretary Lewis to see Reinsch with twenty demands and asked him whether the information he had received about the Twenty-One Demands came directly from Yuan Shikai. In his answer to Lewis, Reinsch revealed a sentence, implying that he had spoken to Yuan Shikai once. He also told Lewis that he had taken pictures of the Japanese version of the Twenty-One Demands and translated them into English. He took the Twenty-One Demands that Lewis had brought to another room to compare them with his translation. He told Lewis, "Bishop Favre took these Twenty-One Demands to see Heki. Don't be afraid that he will accuse Bishop Favre of intentionally slandering Japan."

Then I went to see Heki. After exchanging greetings, I directly discussed the Twenty-One Demands with him. I said that it would be easy for Japan to occupy the coastal ports of China and Beijing. However, since Japan obtained Taiwan in 1896, it has not completely conquered it. Although Taiwan is just a small island with a railway, Japan would have to rely on military force to maintain it. Japan has spent twenty years of operation and still cannot conquer an island with a population of three million. How long would it take Japan to conquer the entire China with a population of 400 million?

I further pointed out several facts and said to him that in the seventeenth century, the people of Sichuan revolted against the Qing Dynasty and it was not until a quarter of them died that the rebellion was suppressed. Now Sichuan has a population of 68 million, 1,500 miles from the coast and 1,000 miles from the nearest railway. I recently visited Sichuan and the anti-Japanese sentiment in the province is strong. If Sichuan Province is determined to fight to the death, Japan will not be able to conquer it even if it uses troops for half a century. Furthermore, the Taiping Rebellion lasted for more than ten years and resulted in the deaths of 20 million people before it was quelled. I said to Heki earnestly that China is a vast country with a large population, and the people are determined to die. If they engage in guerrilla warfare with the Japanese, Japan will never have any hope of annexing China. Even the great powers will never allow Japan to control China and endanger world peace. Even if Japan swallows China, I believe that the great powers will definitely force Japan to withdraw from China, just like the story of forcing Japan to withdraw from the Liaodong Peninsula in 1896. I hope that Japan will not bring disgrace upon itself. Moreover, Japan is now heavily in debt. It would be best to follow the example of Britain and strive to develop its industry and commerce.

Several hundred stones of Changshu and Xixi Beigeng rice in upper-class warehouses were priced similarly to the previous market. Early and late season rice was firm, while secondary rice was weak. Foreign Du Jian and Bianyin Yuanwei were weak and showing signs of falling.

About 14 or 15 rice boats carrying Changshu and Xixi clams arrived in the North Shanghai market. Transactions in urban and rural areas were not very lively. Thick-stalked rice arrivals sold flat, with no rise or fall. Thin rice was handled by visiting traders, with a starting price one chi higher. New stalk and new visitor tip arrivals sold sluggishly, and the situation returned to weakening.

Hunan Rice Continues to Arrive in Shanghai 197

A Large Batch to Arrive Soon

Foreign Rice Remains Stable

Yesterday, foreign rice sales stalled, but this street continued to have demand. This street, along with rural villages and scattered households, sold one lot of Saigon rice with 500 bags, priced at 9.65 to 9.6 yuan, and 2,000 bags of small-grain rice, priced at 9.15 to 9.05 yuan. In addition, old small-grain rice was priced at 8.95 yuan. Yesterday, another 150 bags of Hunan rice arrived, also handled by Yu Feng, but no transactions were made due to disagreements on price. However, according to news from Hunan traders, a large batch is expected to arrive in Shanghai in the next week, about 3,000 bags. Their costs are lower, with high-quality rice around 9 yuan, and medium and secondary rice at 9 to 8.5 yuan. The continuous wind and rain yesterday suggested the possibility of a typhoon, so public sentiment had already settled down.

Flour Market Enters a Weak Trend 198

After the opening of the flour market yesterday morning, the prices for each month showed an initial stabilization followed by a weakening trend. Because foreign wheat quotations were lower by about 0.1 to 0.2 yuan, the opening momentum was not firm. Later, due to factories stopping and waiting to see if outside clients would sell, there were slight purchases of near and far terms, which recovered slightly. The afternoon opening was the opposite of the morning. Initially, people's sentiment was still firm due to the good morning, but large factories continued to sell, so the market weakened again (Fook Kan Wheat No. 2 was quoted at 3 taels 8 qian 7 fen). Seeing factories continuously selling, on one hand, it was because the price of foreign wheat was fixed, and on the other hand, it was because the inventory was very large, and they had no choice but to sell it off. As a result, the current month remained unchanged, September fell by 0.05 li, October fell by 0.1 fen, November fell by 0.075 fen, December fell by 0.125 fen, and January fell by 0.1 fen.

Futures Wheat Still Tends to Be Firm 199

After the opening of the futures wheat market yesterday morning and afternoon, the prices for each month generally remained bullish. Although foreign wheat quotations were lower by about 0.1 to 0.2 yuan, market sentiment was that what was fixed for foreign wheat belonged to the factories, and there was no reason for the exchange to sell both flour wheat. Therefore, the position of domestic wheat remained firm. Kaitai Run bought in this month, preparing to receive goods, so it broke through the 5-qian mark again. September and October generally hovered, but the trend was still good. As a result, this month rose by 0.3 fen compared to the previous day, September and October remained unchanged, November rose by 0.3 fen, and December fell by 0.1 fen. Spot wheat was quiet due to lack of arrivals and sales, and only bales remained unopened.

Sugar Market: Raw and White Sugar Turns Stable After Falling 200

Over 50,000 Bags of Dutch Red Arrived Yesterday

Yesterday, the sugar market's trading at the Sugar Association's market remained quiet. The price of Dutch No. 24 raw white sugar turned stable after falling, with the transaction price falling to 14 taels, 3 qian, and 7.5 fen. Over a thousand bags were traded, but the output was not high. Demand was still strong, and the trend was quite promising. No. 22 medium white sugar was 14 taels, No. 8 Dutch red sugar was 10 taels, 0 qian, and 4.75 fen, slightly higher at 10 taels, 0 qian, and 5.25 fen, and No. 10 goods were 10 taels, 0 qian, and 9.75 fen. The market situation was still stable, but the arrival of over 51,000 bags by the Jianyuan Company on the "Zhisaluya" ship slightly calmed the market. Taikoo Sugar B Mark was quoted at 16 taels and 2 qian, CW Mark at 15 taels, 6 qian, and 7.5 fen, DY Mark at 15 taels, 4 qian, and 2.5 fen, H Mark at 12 taels and 4 qian. In and out were still active, and the market situation was quite stable.

North-South Goods: Hainan Longan Turns from Weak to Rise 201

The previous batch of Hainan longan was oversupplied, causing the market price to plummet, and the cargo owners all suffered losses. Therefore, the number of arrivals in this batch was greatly reduced, totaling only over 200 pieces. A portion of them were released yesterday, and the market price suddenly turned firm and rose. It was reported that high-quality goods opened at 25 taels, and subsequently decreased accordingly, an increase of 2 or 3 taels compared to the previous market.

Silk and Tea: Huangbai Factory Sells Clean, Prices Rise 202

Yesterday, the silk market in this port negotiated with European and American firms for silk from Huangbai factories. Chinese silk merchants insisted on high prices, and transactions were difficult to complete. Yesterday, Jardine Matheson and Blue, Yue, and Bi sold 40 packages of Shanghai white factory silk of upper-grade B (suitable for British sales) at 680 taels (suitable for British sales) , 30 packages of medium-grade silk of 20-22 strips at 565 taels, (suitable for French sales) and 60 packages of medium-grade silk of 83.4 average at 623 taels. (suitable for American sales) 40 packs of Chuanchang iron silk, with 13-15 stripes in the upper body, sold for 620 taels, and 20 packs of wood silk sold for 535 taels.

Xiuning Autumn Tea Production is Scarce 203

Autumn tea (namely, Autumn White Dew) is the third time the tea tree sprouts. Farmers have always been forbidden from picking it. Moreover, because the tea tree's nodes have been picked three times, the barren branches are sparse, and the growth and strength of the spring buds of the following year are weak. Those who have not picked autumn leaves are not able to develop densely. This year, tea farmers in Xiuyi are forced by economic hardship to pick and sell to tea shops any autumn branches that show slight buds. Each household produces about one or two catties per day. It is estimated that the production of autumn tea in the four rural areas of the Xiuning County has been about twenty or thirty dan in the past ten days. The price ranges from 35 yuan to 40 yuan. Tea shops find that this tea has a bright and clear quality, so they are happy to buy it. Unfortunately, the production is scarce, which is not enough to meet the needs of demand.

Zhenmei Green Tea Turns Firm and Smooth 204

Yesterday, Yihai, Jinlong, Xiehe, Tongfu, Yongxing and other firms, as well as the China Tea Company, were all actively searching for Zhenmei green tea from Wuyuan, Tunxi, Shexian, Suian and other routes. The market suddenly became active, and the trading of extracted cores was particularly strong. The opening price was 160 taels, and everyone became firm in the market. In addition, special tea items such as needle eyebrows are also very popular in the market. Among them, goods with excellent leaf quality are sold immediately upon arrival, and the green tea market has shown a firm trend.

Wuyuan Tea Shops Gradually Close 205

Tea shops in Wuyi County, fearing the sluggishness of the Shanghai market this year, have mainly reduced the amount of tea purchased. Except for some tea shops that closed last month, most of those that made two or three shipments have all closed about ten days ago. However, Longteng and Yu Yongxin tea shops in the northern part of the county, as foreign merchants have done business, have recently added more than 100 dan of Gan tea and started picking and manufacturing, which will not be completed until the end of next month. According to the estimates of tea shops that have sold box tea, the difference between sales and costs this year means that each dan of tea has to lose about 30 taels. For the entire Wuyi County, the total loss is at least more than 600,000 yuan.

Fine Cloth Broadcloth: French Goods are Favored

Recently, plain and gray-colored fine cloth has sold well. Kongshi 444 sold for 2 taels and 4 qian, Ningfeng Pengshoutu for 2 taels and 4 qian and a half, and Deji 1313 for 2 taels, 4 qian and 2.5 fen, which is a considerable improvement compared to ten days ago. Those priced at 2 taels are even more popular. French goods, such as those from the Meifa, Yongxing, and Baoduo brands, are quite favored, surpassing other British, German, and American foreign firms. It is said that besides the French foreign firms that have lower-grade broadcloth priced around 2 taels, other firms rarely supply them.

Hardware Factory Adds Four No. White Lead Sheet: The hardware trend is still flat, customer sales are not strong, and factory demand is stagnant, so the market seems to have stalled. Minor decorative purchases have also been very sluggish recently, so the overall situation feels even more deserted. However, the military factory business suddenly picked up yesterday. Over two hundred bundles of Four No. white lead sheets were released yesterday, and the market goods were almost completely searched out. Due to the empty Bu Xiu, it is estimated that each dan can be valued at 22 taels and 5 qian, an increase of more than 1 tael compared to before. However, the bottom storage is surprisingly dry, and if another batch is processed later, the market situation may rise again.

Supplement to the Shanghai Shen Bao

Comments

Like Father, Like Son 206

— Buddha

Yesterday, the Shanghai newspapers reported that Gu Chengyou, the son of Gu Zhenxian, the compradore of Mitsui & Co., warned his father Zhenxian to resign from his position as compradore, which angered his father, leading to his expulsion and subsequent mental disorder. He was detained for buying things. The report generally stated as such. From the old perspective, this is naturally a major upheaval of ethics. From the new perspective, it is a manifestation of patriotic enthusiasm. Is it a major upheaval or enthusiasm? A clear explanation should be given. Because now is an era of unclear right and wrong, and lack of reason, the truth of everything should be clarified.

I do not know the inside story of Gu Chengyou's warning to his father, nor do I know the general public's evaluation. I cannot help but criticize the situation as presented by this incident and the current morbid mentality of young people in society. Gu Zhenxian worked as a compradore for a Japanese firm. After the September 18th Incident, he refused to resign. After the January 28th Incident, he still refused to resign. Gu Zhenxian was blinded by greed and willing to be a traitorous merchant. This ironclad case is undeniable.

But who is Chengyou? He is the son of Gu Zhenxian. The ancients said that one should gently advise one's parents. "Gently" means subtly. Now that the old etiquette has been overthrown, the word "subtly" is naturally no longer applicable. Now, Chengyou advises his father, but he does not listen. He warns him in the name of the Iron Blood Corps, but he still does not listen. Gu Zhenxian prioritizes profit and has lost all conscience. He is indeed despised by humanity. However, Chengyou and Zhenxian still have some blood relationship. Assuming that Gu Chengyou could truly renounce his father for righteousness and was unwilling to be the son of a traitorous merchant, he should publish a statement in the newspaper, sever his father-son relationship, and seek a new life on his own. This would also be a bright path.

Now, Chengyou goes to Wing On Company to select goods and sends them home, only to have them returned once and then sent again a second time. In Chengyou's mind, he naturally wants to mess with his family, not the company. However, the company has suffered many troubles and should settle the account with him. However, I have observed that many young people now have extravagant habits and demand things from their fathers. When their demands are not met, they borrow names and use threats. This kind of behavior happens often. I do not know what Chengyou's behavior is like on weekdays. However, I believe that Chengyou's behavior of selecting goods and sending them home is not conscious at all and does not resemble what a rational young man would do.

Therefore, loving the country is one thing, and messing up the family is another. It is not that the son of a traitorous merchant opposes his father, so he should be regarded as acting correctly. However, if this kind of behavior comes from the son of a traitorous merchant, it can be regarded as a kind of retribution, as the saying goes, "Like father, like son."

Science

Wireless Electric Light 209

— Deer

[Wireless Telephone] [Wireless Telegraph], we are almost tired of hearing these names, and have seen them countless times. But [Wireless Electric Light], this fresh name, even in this scientifically advanced 20th century, is still only a dream. Now I suddenly write this strange topic, I think everyone will be surprised, or want to be suspicious, saying it's just renaming [Flashlight] [Gasoline Lamp] [Kerosene Lamp] [::::]! But what I call [Wireless Electric Light] is not what you guessed. Now let me slowly explain.

Originally, an electric light is a device that emits light by conducting current through two wires to a light bulb. Everyone knows this, and there's no need for me to explain it. What I call [Wireless Electric Light] is also such a device, but the current it needs is conducted from two wires so thin that they are almost invisible, almost like wireless. In essence, it is still a wired electric light, just an interesting scientific trick, or to put it bluntly, just fooling people!

The method is very simple. Just find an old flower wire (length doesn't matter), and carefully scrape off the gauze and rubber covering it with a small knife, being careful not to cut the copper wire inside. After scraping it clean, separate the copper wire into strands, and twist every two strands together (because a single strand is too thin and easily breaks). Do the same to make two long strands (the length depends on the distance from the power source). After twisting them, apply some glue to each strand to prevent them from splitting. Then take an ordinary large light bulb and a light socket, and a foot or so of flower wire. That's all the materials you need.

Just connect the two ends of one end of the flower wire to the light socket: then install the light bulb, and slowly separate the two ends of the other end in a staggered pattern, until the two ends are about three or four inches apart, so they don't touch each other: then nail them to the wall near the table, and cover the wire part with paper, so others won't notice it. Place the light bulb on the table: then connect one end of the two thin copper wires to the two ends of the other end of the short flower wire, and connect the other two ends of the thin copper wires to the current-carrying wires: (Be sure to turn off the main switch when connecting, and keep the two strands several inches apart to avoid danger). The route it passes through must be along the wall or other stable places, not suspended in the air, to prevent danger. If there are turns or damp places in the route, you can insulate them with insulators, or first use the complete rubber rings scraped from the flower wire, and put them on the thin wires, and place them separately in these places. The entire installation is now complete!

But you still need to carefully check if there are any improprieties. If there are none, you can turn on the switch, and the light will naturally turn on! (The brightness is comparable to a lamp powered by ordinary thick wires). If you install it very well and properly, then no one will understand your secret, unless you tell them: This kind of electric light, although wired, seems like wireless, so that's why I say [Wireless Electric Light]! Readers may say [Slippery fellow] at this point! Haha!

Society Improvement Discussion Group

My Opinion on Daycare Centers 210

— Zu'e

Your proposal for [Daycare Centers] is excellent. Not hesitating about my own shallowness, I will also talk about this matter.

It can be said that daycare centers already have facilities in China, namely, orphanages. However, this kind of facility is entirely charitable in nature and exists within certain limits, so the aims are different, and the content is not handled properly. Many malpractices arise, so they attract little attention and are not improved.

Originally, the prevalence of orphanages can be said to be ubiquitous in our country. This kind of extremely good social welfare undertaking, if it can be utilized and improved, is truly a wonderful thing.

Daycare facilities are needed when parents are engaged in social undertakings or have other entanglements and cannot attend to the task of raising children. By using a group management method, they take on an obligation – that is, giving a considerable amount of money to the daycare center – to settle the infants, so they can concentrate on their own undertakings. This method is indeed a new discovery in the new society. However, the establishment of daycare centers is difficult to realize without a sound society. Soviet Russia has a different organization and social situation, so babies there can be entrusted to the public from birth. Their orphanages are set up in factories, schools, public entertainment places, or parks. In a considerable process, they enter kindergarten, elementary school, middle school, and even university, without you having to worry about anything, because although they still have individual families in form, the focus of everyone has already shifted to the social public. However, in China, the situation is naturally different, but with the inability to balance career and parenting, the need for daycare centers is indeed urgent! In my humble opinion, the existing orphanages should be thoroughly changed and made scientific and social. I record the following suggestions for improvement:

The original purpose of orphanages was: to take in and raise babies who were born but could not be raised and were about to be abandoned. On the one hand, the remaining babies are provided to those who have no children to adopt. This spirit should naturally not be abandoned, but it can be renamed [Charitable Department of Daycare Center], which is dedicated to carrying out this aim. In addition, it is dedicated to raising children for others, and there must be a considerable price. For example, how much should be paid for each child entrusted to be raised each year? The center should determine it in detail, and collect a certain amount on top of the various expenses as a fund for the charitable department (or fundraising may be done separately).

The management method should of course be as perfect as possible. The past corruption in the management of orphanages was really unpopular. Like an unsound wet nurse, feeding many babies, or a stupid and barbaric woman, acting as a nanny, these can affect the happiness of children. Therefore, wet nurses, nannies, etc. must receive considerable education or training. Other requirements include spacious and clean housing, and large gardens and open spaces. In short, everything that is beneficial to children should be as perfect as possible (but it should not be too aristocratic! Otherwise, will it not affect the children themselves?)

These are my opinions on changing orphanages to daycare centers. First, it is easier to use the existing scope of orphanages to expand them. Second, the organization of the daycare center still does not abandon the original charitable nature of the orphanage, achieving two things at once, perhaps here? I hope everyone will discuss it.

A Corner of Society

The Barber's Words 211

— Yi Yong

Elementary School Teachers Lament Their Inferiority

Yesterday I went to get a haircut, and I asked the barber, [How much do you earn each month?] The barber said, [About forty or fifty dollars]. I was a little surprised when I heard this, so I asked him how he could earn forty or fifty dollars a month. The barber said, [On average, we can give haircuts to eleven or twelve customers a day. At two dimes per person, that's two dollars and forty cents. After a four-six split with the boss, we can earn one dollar and forty-four cents a day. Wouldn't that be more than forty dollars a month? And the boss provides the meals. But when I look at the schoolteachers, elementary school teachers earn ten or twenty dollars a month, and some middle school teachers earn only about forty dollars. And they have to pay for their own meals, which cost at least six or seven dollars. They actually earn less than us, but they have to spend a lot of capital. What capital do we have to speak of? They still often engage in infighting and make trouble. It's really not as peaceful as us. So although our position is lower, we are still in the same profession. There is no high or low in a profession, and we are also very comforted]. After listening to his words, I couldn't help but sigh lightly, what's the use of studying, why do we study, alas! Elementary school teachers are really inferior to a barber.

Page 20

School Photo

Whose Fault? 212

— Zhong Na

Before the summer vacation, when a certain middle school in this city was about to hold the graduation examination, a certain student gathered his usual good classmates at his home for a secret meeting. He acted as the chairman and announced the purpose of the meeting: [Now the graduation examination is coming soon. The grades of several of us friends are not very good. If we can't graduate this time, wouldn't it be very unlucky?]

[Yes,] Student A interjected: [Then we have no other way but to burn the midnight oil].

[Is there still time to burn the midnight oil?] Student B seemed to understand Student A's intention and said: [If you want to burn the midnight oil, you can go alone. I am most unwilling to burn the midnight oil].

[Listen to me,] Student A said with a grin: [I have an excellent method! As long as you follow my method, I guarantee that you will all graduate].

[What method? What method?] They all hurriedly asked.

[There are three school workers in the school who mimeograph the exam papers. As long as we give them some money, we can ask them to steal the exam papers in advance. Isn't this method good? About ten dollars per person is enough. A total of thirty dollars. We six people can share it. Each person only needs five dollars. Is it convenient or not?]

[This method is excellent!] Everyone agreed.

After the three school workers each put two five-dollar bills in their pockets, physics, chemistry, history: : :

Exam papers flew out one by one. As a result of the examination, these six friends, whose grades were usually not good, did surprisingly well this time. The principal was somewhat suspicious, and the other school workers who could not get a share became jealous after seeing the money and revealed the secret. The principal put on the airs of a lord and summoned the three school workers for a strict interrogation. They all admitted to accepting bribes and cheating. So these three poor, ignorant school workers were immediately fired under the principal's thunderous anger. But these six students, due to various relationships, were still allowed to graduate: they were still given the same graduation.

Whose fault is this after all? It's not the fault of the six students, nor is it the fault of the three unlucky school workers. It is really the fault of the school authorities: especially the director of moral education. The occurrence of this unfortunate event can be said to be the school having no moral education, or it can be said that the school's moral education is completely bankrupt!

Gao Wang's Applies for Divorce Recording 255

Noted from the petition. According to Article 1050 of the Civil Code, a voluntary divorce should be in writing and should have the signatures of two or more witnesses. The divorce agreement submitted by the applicant only has one lawyer's witness, which is not in accordance with the law. The request for recording cannot be approved.
